called فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ in Arabic, the course is compulsory for the students.
As a beginner, you should take note of the development and the importance of فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ .
In the first and second centuries of Islam,فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ was developed amongst the series of subjects developed by Muslims to preserve and understand the language of the Qur’an – Arabic.
Mu‘ādh bn Muslim al–Ħarrāī is recognized as the exponent ofفُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ .
Another school of thought attributes its development to ‘Alī bn Abī Tālib.
So far, فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ has proven to be an extraordinary mechanism of enriching Arabic language as you will see it practically as we enter into the nitty-grity of فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ Course Aims ARA381 aims at ensuring your ability to: • comprehend the position of فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ in the entire Arabic Studies; • identify the scope of فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ ; • employ the available mechanism to conjugate verbs and nouns; • state the relationship betweenفُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ and (cid:8)(cid:9)ْ (cid:10)َand • employ various available patterns inفْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ to enrich your language acquisition skill.
4Course Objectives To accomplish the above aims, you have a golden opportunity in the series of objectives which are divided into two, namely short term and long term.
While short term objectives revolve around immediate accomplishment i.e.
what you are able to attain at the end of each unit, the long term objectives indicate your demonstration of mastery of فْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ .
In technical terms, your short term objectives are called behavioural objectives.
Such objectives are meant to measure the extent to which you have benefited from the unit lesson just taught.
In other words the extent you can recall, state, comprehend, or perform any prescribed task on just concluded lesson.
On the other hand, the long term objectives are futuristic i.e.
they revolve around your ability to permanently retain the conjugation of verbs from ضِ (cid:13)(cid:14)َto(cid:4)(cid:14)ْ أَ or noun from د(cid:4)َْ(cid:17)(cid:14)ُ to (cid:18)(cid:19)ْ (cid:20)َ , or the extent you can derive fresh words from their roots such as (cid:21)(cid:22)(cid:23)ا (cid:25)ْ(cid:26)إِ –ن(cid:13)(cid:14)(cid:29)(cid:30)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ –ن(cid:13)(cid:31)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ – (cid:25)(cid:26)إ ل(cid:8)!
(cid:17)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا– "#(cid:13)(cid:17)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إetc.
based on the skills acquired during the course.
You are hereby expected to be able to: • describe the scope of فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ ; • state what فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ and (cid:8)(cid:9)ْ (cid:10)َhave in common; • conjugate verbs; • enrich and enlarge your vocabulary base through derivatives known as ; and • use in sentences the newly acquired words 2 Working Through this Course ARA381 is made up of 12 units, carefully packaged to enable you to learn فُ ْ(cid:4)(cid:6)َ without tears.
Basically, you are expected to study all units in addition to any other books as may be recommended by NOUN.
As you progress in this course, you will find Assessment exercise specially designed to enable you to gage your level of attainment of the behavioural objectives.
Further more, at the end of every unit, you will required to submit written assignments for assessment purposes.
You will also write a final examination at the end of this course.

Assignment Files In this file, you will find all the details of the work you must submit to your tutor for marking.
The marks you obtain from these assignments will count towards the final mark you obtain for this course.
You will find further information or assignments in the Assignment file itself and later in this Course Guide in the section on assignment.
Presentation Schedule 7 The presentation schedule included in your course materials gives you the important dates for the completion of Tutor – Marked Assignment and attending tutorials.
Remember, you are required to submit all your assignments by the due date.
You should guard against falling behind in your work.
Assessment Your assessment will be based on Tutor-Marked Assignments (TMAs) and a final examination you will write at the end of the course.
Tutor – Marked Assignments (TMAs) Every unit contains at least one or two assignments.
You are advised to work through all the assignments and submit for assessment.
Your tutor will assess the assignments and select four which will constitute the 30% of your final grade.
The Tutor – Marked Assignments may be presented to you in a separate file.
Just know that for every unit there are some Tutor – Marked Assignments for you.
It is important you do them and submit for assessment.
Final Examination and Grading At the end of the course, you will write a final examination which shall last for two hours, you will be requested to answer three questions out of at least five questions.

This is because you can read and work through specially designed study materials at your own pace, and at a time and place that suit you best.
Think of it as reading the lecture instead of listening to the lecturer.
In the same way a lecturer might give you some reading to do, the study units tell you when to read, and which are your text materials or set books.
You are provided exercises to do at appropriate points, just as a lecturer might give you an in – class exercise.
Each of the study units follows a common format.
The first item is an introduction to the other units and the course as a whole.
Next to this is a set of learning objectives.
These objectives let you know what you should be able to do by the time you have completed the unit.
These learning objectives are meant to guide your study.
The moment a unit is finished, you must go back and check whether you have achieved the objectives.
If this is made a habit, then you will significantly improve your chances of passing the course.
The main body of the 6 unit guides you through the required reading from other sources.
This will usually be either from your set books or from Reading section.
The following is a practical strategy for working through the course.
If you run into any trouble, telephone your tutor.
Remember that your tutor’s job is to help you.
When you need assistance, do not hesitate to call and ask your tutor to provide it.
1.
Read this Course Guide thoroughly, it is your first assignment 2.
Organize a study schedule.
Design a “Course Overview” to guide you through the course.
Note the time you are expected to spend on each unit and how the assignments relate to the unit.
Important information, e.g.
details of your tutorials, and the date of the first day of the semester is available from the study centre.
You need to gather all the information into one place, such as your diary or a wall calendar.
Whatever method you choose to use, you should decide on and write your own date’s schedule of work for each unit.
3.
Once you have created your own schedule, do everything to stay faithful to it.
The major reason that students fail is that they get behind with their course work.
If you get into difficulties with your schedule, please, let your tutor know before it is too late for help.
4.
Turn to unit 1, and read the introduction and the objectives for the unit.
5.
Assemble the study materials.
You will need your set books and the unit you are studying at any point in time.
6.
Work through the unit.
As you work through the unit, you will know what sources to consult for further information.
127.
Keep in touch with your study centre.
Up – to – date course information will be continuously available there.
8.
Well before the relevant due dates (about 4 weeks before due dates); keep in mind that you will learn a lot by doing the assignment carefully.
They have been designed to help you meet the objectives of the course and, therefore, will help you pass the examination.
Submit all assignments not later than the due date.
9. Review the objectives for each study unit to confirm that you have achieved them.
If you feel unsure about any of the objectives, review the study materials or consult your tutor.
7 10.
When you are confident that you have achieved a unit’s objectives, you can start on the next unit proceed unit by unit through the course and try to pace your study so that you keep yourself on schedule.
11.
When you have submitted an assignment to your tutor for marking, do not wait for its return before starting on the next unit.
Keep to your schedule.
When the assignment returned, pay particular attention to your tutor’s comments, both on the tutor-marked assignment form and also the written comments on the ordinary assignments.
12.
After completing the last unit, review the course and prepare yourself for the final examination.
Check that you have achieved the unit objectives (listed at the beginning of each unit) and the course objectives (listed in the course guide).
Facilitators/Tutors and Tutorials The dates; times and locations of these will be made available to you, together with the name, telephone number and the address of your tutor.
Each assignment will be marked by your tutor.
Pay close attention too the comments your tutor might make on your assignments as these will help in your progress make sure that assignments reach your tutor on or before the due date.
Your tutorials are important; therefore try not to skip any.
It is an opportunity to meet your tutor and your fellow students.
It is also an opportunity to get the help of your tutor and discuss any difficulties encountered on your reading.
Summary In ARA381: Arabic Morphology, you are taken through different aspects of ف(cid:4)(cid:6).
To a large extent, ف(cid:4)(cid:6) is simplified for you.
It is made easy.
Words/terms such as Q(cid:22)إ ن(cid:13)(cid:31)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ ,ل(cid:8)!
(cid:17)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ ,"#(cid:13)(cid:17)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ ,(cid:25)(cid:26)إ ,"!+ ,(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)آetc.
are defined.
Where necessary, terms with technical connotation are described with illustrations.
For example, terms such ت(cid:13);0<(cid:19)(cid:22)ا(derivatives) where they are derived from, common ground between ف(cid:4)(cid:6)and (cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10)are explained with illustrations.
Conjugation as the core of ف(cid:4)(cid:6)is extensively explained across the units of the course.
However, your ability to conjugate, define, describe, and illustrate in sentences depends on your taking maximum advantage of the Course Guide which accompanies this Course Material.

Unit 1 Definition of Ṣarf ف(cid:4)$(cid:22)ا %&(cid:4)!'
1.0 Introduction 2.0 Objectives 3.0 Main Content 3.1 Definition of Ṣarf ف(cid:4)$(cid:22)ا %&(cid:4)!'
3.2 The Scope of Ṣarf ف(cid:4)$(cid:22)ا ل(cid:13).
(cid:14) 3.3 Similarity between Ṣarf and Nahw (cid:8)(cid:9)F(cid:22)او ف(cid:4)$(cid:22)ا ,2N 3N(cid:13)<0(cid:22)ا 4.0 Conclusion 5.0 Summary 6.0 Tutor Marked Assignment 7.0 References/Further Reading 1.0 Introduction Morphology, (ف(cid:4)(cid:6)), was introduced within the array of language studies which include Grammar,((cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10)) Rhetoric,((cid:21)T7N) Philology ((cid:21)B(cid:30)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:30)#), Phonetics (cid:25)(cid:30)#) (تا(cid:8)(cid:6))ا, etc.
The main motivation for the development/introduction of these language studies was the preservation of the Qur’ān – which was revealed in Arabic – in terms of its ensuring its correct reading and accurate understanding of its message.
It should be noted that the language studies of which ف(cid:4)(cid:6) formed a part came within the context of the complete change brought by Islam to the life of the Arabs in the Arabian Peninsula.
It was a total transformation of life which means a sharp shift from the prevailing Jahiliyyah culture to civilization and urbanization spanning across social, commercial, judicial and religious aspects of life in the first and second centuries of Hijrah corresponding with seventh and eighth centuries of the Christian Era (CE).
Since ف(cid:4)(cid:6) came as a branch of language studies, little wonder that it shares a lot with other branches especially (cid:8)(cid:9)ـ(cid:10) (Grammar) which is explained below.
Against this background, our attention in this unit is focused on definition of ف(cid:4)(cid:6), its scope and what it shares in common with (cid:8)(cid:9)ـ(cid:10).
2.0 Objectives At the end of this unit, you should be able to: • defineف(cid:4)(cid:6) ; • describe the scope ofف(cid:4)(cid:6) ; and • state similarities and dissimilarities between ف(cid:4)(cid:6) and Nahw.

(cid:4)2Bِ$a (cid:22)ا 3ُFَNْإِ .3ِ0ِ!َ(cid:14)ِ(cid:13)(cid:20)َ X+ِ (cid:13)&jرِْودَ By definition, Morphology, simply called ف(cid:4)(cid:6) in Arabic is the study of the structural formation of words and the cases that affect the formation.
The literal meaning of ف(cid:4)(cid:6) is indicative of what Morphology is all about.
Literally, ف(cid:4)(cid:6) means to change i.e.
to change from one form to another form.
Technically, ف(cid:4)(cid:6) means a structural change affecting a word called (cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)آ from one form to another form or to several forms.
For instance, you will observe in the above text how the word ^َ 0َآَ changed from one form to several forms.
The word ^َ 0َآَ (to write) has structurally changed severally e.g.

to correspond with e.g.

Kalmah which means a word is of three types; namely ٌ"!ْ+ِ (verb) ٌ(cid:25)ْ(cid:26)إِ (noun) ٌفْ(cid:4)Aَ (particle) Examples: ٌ"ْ!+ِ ٌ(cid:25)(cid:26)ْ إِ ٌفْ(cid:4)Aَ 15 بَ (cid:4)َ>َ to beat ٌ5(cid:22)َوَ a boy ْ,(cid:14)ِ from lَ (cid:30)َ(cid:20)َ to seat ٌ(cid:29)ْCVُ bread X(cid:22)َإِ to سَ رَدَ to study ٌب(cid:13)0َآِ a book X+ِ in Of all the three types of Kalmah listed above, ف(cid:4)(cid:6) covers verbs and nouns to the exclusion of particles.
The question you may ask then is: what does ف(cid:4)(cid:6) do to verbs and nouns?
The answer is, simply put, %ُ &(cid:4)ِْ$'َ which means structural transformation of verbs and nouns into various shapes and forms.
It should be quickly noted that the structural transformation we are talking about is for a purpose which is the reflection of different meanings and situations sometimes tied up to periodization.
When %ُ &(cid:4)ِ$ْ 'َ takes its toll on verbs and nouns, they (verbs and nouns) are called (cid:21)+(cid:4)$0(cid:14) i.e.
(cid:21)+(cid:4)$0(cid:14) ل(cid:13)!+أ and (cid:21)+(cid:4)$0(cid:14) ء(cid:13)(cid:19)(cid:26)أ.
This is a situation when a verb is conjugated such as conjugating a verb from past tense (ضٍ (cid:13)(cid:14)َ), present tense (ٌعرِ(cid:13)gَ (cid:14)ُ), and command i.e.
future tense ((cid:4)ُْ(cid:14)أَ).
When noun is taken through the same process of %&(cid:4)$' i.e.
conjugation, it changes from singular (د(cid:4)(cid:17)(cid:14)), dual (XFM(cid:14)) and plural ((cid:18)(cid:19)(cid:20)).

163.3 Between Ṣarf and Nahw ف(cid:4)(cid:6) and Nahw in terms of their functions are like a pair of scissors in which one tongue cannot function alone without the other tongue.
Both ف(cid:4)(cid:6) and Nahw complement each other in preserving the Arabic language and ultimately guide the learner towards making correct and intelligible sentences.
So, what they both share in common is the role of preserving the language through application of their rules and regulations.
However, in terms of the scope of operation, they differ significantly as illustrated in the text below.

In the same token, nouns such as: مv)ُ ْا ،نُ (cid:13)آa5v(cid:22)ا ،(cid:21)ُFَ&5َِ(cid:19)ْ(cid:22)ا ،(cid:25)v!َْ(cid:22)ا ،(cid:21)ُ(cid:19)a!َ(cid:22)ْا ،(cid:21)ُ&َْ(cid:4);َْ(cid:22)ا ،^ُ &(cid:4)ِ;َْ(cid:22)ا ،عُ (cid:8)C(cid:26)ْ )ُ ْا ،(cid:21)ُ(cid:26)َ رَْ5(cid:19)َْ(cid:22)ا change from one form to another to reflect number.
This constant change is known as %ُ &(cid:4)ِْ$'َ (deletion) and it applies to both ٌل(cid:13)!َْ+أَ and ٌء(cid:13)(cid:19)َ(cid:26)ْ أَ.

The English term declension is used to denote both %ُ &(cid:4)ِ$ْ 'َ and بُ ا(cid:4)َ#ْ إِ.
While %ُ &(cid:4)ِ$ْ 'َ 17means structural transformation of a verb or noun as illustrated in the two tables above, بُ ا(cid:4)َ#ْ إِ means changes that occur in the vowels at the end of a word be it verb or noun.
The vowels that are amenable to changes are Dammah ــُـ Fathah ــَـ Kasrah ــِـ and Sukun ـْــ.

By now, the distinction between ف(cid:4)(cid:6) and (cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10) must have been crystal clear to you.
For example, while ف(cid:4)(cid:6) with its rules governs the act of changing the words (i.e "!ـ+ وأ ،(cid:25)ـ(cid:26)إ :(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)آ,) from one form to another, (cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10) takes the control of alteration of vowel at the end of words in accordance with the prevailing case.
Basically, both (cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10) and ف(cid:4)(cid:6)are supposed to guide you to make correct statement with a view to accurately reflecting the intended meaning and situations correctly.
One point of observation, you should recall that ف(cid:4)(cid:9)(cid:22)ا the particle is the third member of the (cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)آ family.
But it is not governed by any regulation that will make it change its form.
It has a lone structure that never changes.
Unlike the nature of "!ـ+ and (cid:25)ـ(cid:26)إ the particle such as X(cid:30)َ#َ ،X(cid:22)َإِ ،=+ِ ،نa إِ ،نa أَ are free fron any rule that could either change their forms or their vowels.

18 194.0 Conclusion ف(cid:4)(cid:6) and (cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10) have one thing in common; namely preservation of Arabic Language through provision of rules and regulations that guide the learner of the language to make flawless and intelligible expressions.
Further more, both of them have (cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)(cid:31)(cid:22)ا (word) as the area of operation.
But while ف(cid:4)(cid:6) deals with the structural transformation of the words into various shapes and forms, (cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10) deals with the changes that occur in the vowels especially at the end of the word ( (cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)(cid:31)(cid:22)ا (cid:4)Vاوأ ) 5.0 Summary This Unit introduced Ṣarf (Arabic Morphology) to you as the study of the structural changes taking place in words with a view to creating various meanings from one single root.
It showed how both ف(cid:4)(cid:6) and (cid:8)(cid:9)(cid:10) take the (cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)آ as their area of oppration.
It gives coupious examples as illustration and provides you with self assessment exercises so that you will be able to know your level of understanding.
The conclusion highlights the main point discussed.

The purity of the د(cid:4).

Such letters are called Radicals to the extent that they are all original to that verb and each of them is indispensable for the verb will be rendered meaningless, should any of the letters be omitted e.g.
: ^آر.
Take the verb ^آر which means he took a ride, should letter ر be omitted the rest two letters ^آ becomes meaningless or at least the remaining two letters cannot mean to take a ride.

A verb is described as al-Mazid feehi if it contains one or more additional letters to the original component ones which are known as foundation radicals.

An example of al-Mazeed thulaathiyy is "َ 'َ(cid:13)[َ with the additional ة5(cid:14) %(cid:22)أ to "َ 0َ[َ.
It can also become "َ 'َ(cid:13);َ'َ as ت and ة5(cid:14) %(cid:22)أ are added.

5.0 Summary The distinction between د(cid:4).
(cid:19)(cid:22)ا and 5&(cid:29)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا is that every letter in the د(cid:4).
(cid:19)(cid:22)ا is original and cannot be dropped without disrupting the meaning of the verb.
For example, if a letter is removed from l(cid:30)(cid:20) e.g.
ج the remaining l(cid:22) have no meaning.
In case of 5&(cid:29)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا removing a letter or more can only change the meaning but not to render the verb meaningless e.g.
if %(cid:22)أ is removed from "'(cid:13)[ you still have "0[ which is meaningful i.e.
he killed though it is different from the meaning of "'(cid:13)[.
Generally, 5&(cid:29)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا is advantageous in terms of widening the scope if verbs as a verb through ةد(cid:13)&ز can produce various meaning.

4.0 Conclusion You will observe that in the conjugation ofX(cid:26)ا5k(cid:22)ا "!
(cid:17)(cid:22)ا , it is only verbs of "!
(cid:17)0(cid:26)ا scale that have 3N ل(cid:8)!(cid:17)(cid:14).
Others do not have 3N ل(cid:8)!(cid:17)(cid:14).
But how do you know the verb with 3N ل(cid:8)!
(cid:17)(cid:14) and those that do not have?
The surest mechanism is through the meaning.
For example, if you say ‘I laughed and I drank’.
In the first sentence, you just laugh and the action of laughter ends with you.
Whereas, in the second sentence, you drank; you must have drunk some liquid, water, tea or milk.
So, to drink بُ (cid:4)َْ<&َ needs 3N ل(cid:8)!
(cid:17)(cid:14) while to laugh fَ (cid:9)ِ >َ does not require 3N ل(cid:8)!(cid:17)(cid:14).
5.0 Summary In this unit, you have been taken through ل(cid:13)!+)ا نازوأ from three lettered to six lettered ones.
And the mechanism of conjugation has been sufficiently treated.
However, your ability to navigate conveniently in the aspects of ف(cid:4)(cid:6) we have treated so far requires extensive reading because some aspects of ف(cid:4)(cid:6) are based on what is known as X#(cid:13)(cid:19)(cid:26) i.e.
oral tradition which does not follow clearly defined patterns or rules.

5.0 Summary 45One peculiarity posed in this segment is that نز(cid:8)‘(cid:22)ا or نازو(cid:23)ا (in its plural form) take shape and status of the نوز(cid:8)‘(cid:19)(cid:22)ا i.e the target verb, For example, if the نوز(cid:8)‘(cid:14) (target verb) is X‘#و which loses its two (cid:21)‘(cid:30)# ف(cid:4)‘A in its (cid:4)‘(cid:14))ا "‘!+ , the two letters will similarly be lost in the (cid:4)‘(cid:14))ا "‘!+ of the نزو.
You must have noticed, therefore, that نزو becomes a follower following the target verb in any situation or case.

(cid:17)(cid:22)ا is the verb that requires an object known as 3‘N ل(cid:8)‘‘!

This is the verb that can not stand with its subject "‘#(cid:13)(cid:17)(cid:22)ا alone without an object i.e 3‘N ل(cid:8)‘!(cid:17)(cid:14).

Oh!
I studied it in reading and not in memorization.

As for me, naturally, I memorized some short chapters which I recite during the five daily obligatory prayers.
I wish I could memorise the Qur'ān as a whole one day and read it excellently well like the young children I saw on the television screen.

Intransitive verb known as مز7‘(cid:22)ا "‘!
(cid:17)(cid:22)ا which is the direct opposite of ى5‘!0(cid:19)(cid:22)ا is treated in this unit.

2.0 Objectives: At the end of this unit, you should be able to: • identify مز7(cid:22)ا "!
(cid:17)(cid:22)ا • utilize the mechanism of changing it to transitive; • conjugate all verbs used for illustration 3.0 Main Content 3.1 مز7(cid:22)ا "!
(cid:17)(cid:22)ا This is the direct opposite of ى5‘!0(cid:19)(cid:22)ا "‘!
(cid:17)(cid:22)ا with which you are already familiar.
"‘!
(cid:17)(cid:22)ا مز 7‘(cid:22)ا is the verb that does not require 3‘N ل(cid:8)‘!
(cid:17)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا in a sentence.
Taste is the main facilitator that assists you to identify مز7‘(cid:22)ا "‘!(cid:17)(cid:22)ا.
For example, if Bilqis is reading and Fatimah is running.
Your taste must tell you that Bilqis must be reading something: a textbook, a news paper, a novel or a letter.
Whatever she is reading is 3‘N ل(cid:8)‘!
(cid:17)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا which means that the verb read is transitive; ى5‘!0(cid:19)(cid:22)ا.
On the other hand, running in the second sentence does not require an object of running as your taste will inform you.
Running begings and ends with the runner.
Therefore, to the extent that the verb run is intransitive مز7(cid:22)ا in Arabic, you say: Bilqis is reading the Qur’an نا(cid:4);(cid:22)ا l2;(cid:30)N أ(cid:4);' Fatimah is running ى(cid:4).'

The first step is to remove (cid:21)c(cid:8)N(cid:4)(cid:14) ء(cid:13)' at the end of the word in question e.g.
ٌ (cid:21)C(cid:22)ِ(cid:13)cَ .
Step two is to add 5(cid:14) %(cid:22)أ + ت to the د(cid:4)(cid:17)(cid:14) i.e.
ٌ^(cid:22)ِ(cid:13)cَ ا + ت = ت(cid:13)Cَ(cid:22)ِ(cid:13)cَ ٌ(cid:21)ـCَآِارَ ا + ت = ٌت(cid:13)Cَآِارَ ٌ(cid:21)(cid:19)َ(cid:30)ِkْ (cid:14)ُ ا + ت = ٌت(cid:13)(cid:19)َ(cid:30)َkْ (cid:14)ُ ٌة5َ(cid:20)ِ (cid:13)(cid:26)َ ا + ت = ٌتا5َ(cid:20)ِ (cid:13)(cid:26)َ ٌ(cid:21)(cid:19)َuِ(cid:13)(cid:6)َ ا + ت = ٌت(cid:13)(cid:19)َuِ(cid:13)(cid:6)َ From the above, you can note that you have no difficulty in formulating (cid:4)آD(cid:14) (cid:18)(cid:19)(cid:20) XFM(cid:14) (cid:25)(cid:22)(cid:13)(cid:26) and (cid:25)(cid:22)(cid:13)(cid:26) L(cid:10)r(cid:14) (cid:18)(cid:19)(cid:20) because in these three cases, the constituent letters are not disrupted.
Incidentally, the (cid:4)ِ2kِ ْ(cid:31)'َ (cid:18)ُ (cid:19)ْ (cid:20)َ (broken plural) poses a unique case.
There is no formula or mechanism to follow or a process to adopt.
Everything is based on oral tradition called X#ِ (cid:13)(cid:19)َ(cid:26)َ .
In this case, the original constituent letters are disrupted and sometimes with additional letters interwoven with the original ones.

That is the surest way to get acquainted with broken plural given the fact that there is no clear formula to use in constructing it (broken plural).

a derivative emanating from teaching and sweeping.
Further more, the object that is being taught or being swept is known in Arabic as (cid:25)(cid:26)إ ل(cid:8)!
(cid:17)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا which is derived from the same root.
This could be seen as a plus for Arabic because while English has the word teacher for the person teaching which is (cid:25)(cid:26)إ "#(cid:13)(cid:17)(cid:22)ا there is no other derivative in English to be taken out of teaching that can be used for the recipient of teaching.
You will note that the word student or learner is the object of teaching.

Self Assessment Exercise Derive from the following routs "#(cid:13)(cid:17)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ, 3N ل(cid:8)!
(cid:17)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ, ن(cid:13)(cid:31)(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ and (cid:21)(cid:22)‰ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ and use them in sentences: ٌ(cid:4)Kْ (cid:26)َ ،ٌlFْآَ ،ٌ^ْهذَ ،ٌ(cid:18)Cْcَ 3.2 (cid:21)CkF(cid:22)او (cid:4)2B$0(cid:22)ا With (cid:21)CkF(cid:22)ا and (cid:4)2B$0(cid:22)ا, you are given an opportunity to manipulate words to express smallness and attribute/ascribe a word to something.
In other words, (cid:4)2B$0(cid:22)ا is used when you want to show how small a thing or person is in the host of his or its pairs.
Similarly, you use (cid:21)CkF(cid:22)ا when you want to attribute something or a person to something else.
There is a pattern i.e.
a type of نزو you use in both cases.
In a three lettered word like ٌ5(cid:22)َوَ , the appropriate نزو is ٌ"2ْ!َ+ُ which gives you ٌ5ْ2(cid:22)َوُ and in the case of a four lettered word, the pattern i.e.
ٌنْزوَ is ٌ"!َ2ْ!َ+ُ in which ٌ(cid:4)(cid:17)َ!ْ(cid:20)َ becomes ٌ(cid:4)(cid:17)َْ2!َ(cid:20)ُ .
In case of (cid:21)CkF(cid:22)ا, you simply add a duplicated ya‘ at the end of the word which you want to attribute.
For example, if you intend attributing a person 67to a town like (cid:4)َ$ْ (cid:14)ِ (Egypt), you simply add a duplicated ya‘ and the word becomes ىp (cid:4)ِ$ْ (cid:14)ِ i.e.
an Egyptian.
Or you intend attributing an action or a dress to a ٌ5(cid:22)َوَ , you add duplicated ya‘ and it becomes ىp 5ِ(cid:22)َوَ i.e.
the action or dress which is that of a boy (5(cid:22)و).

Self Assessment Exercise Attempt making verb our of the following names of towns and places and use them in sentences: سِ (cid:8)Tُ (cid:23)َ – ا5َFَآَ – ْ,Kِ FْEِ اوَ – ْن5َْF(cid:22)َ 4.0 Conclusion Forming verbs out of towns and places should not give you sleepless nights since you do not have a definite formula to work with.
This aspect of ف(cid:4)(cid:6) is to show how flexible Arabic language is and indeed how dynamic and interesting ف(cid:4)(cid:6) is.
5.0 Summary If you take a critical look at (cid:21)َCَْkFd(cid:22)ا, it becomes clear to you that ف(cid:4)(cid:6) is not presenting a unique formula because in English, there is the same formula as you can see in adding n to Nigeria to become Nigerian (e.g.
the Nigerian character)or to America to become American (e.g.
the American embassy).
So, duplicated ya‘ is doing in Arabic what n or ish does in English.
However, there are cases when n cannot apply e.g.
Britain or England, it is ish that is added while the last three letters are removed i.e.
and in England and you have English and ain in Britain and you have British.
You will have similar cases in Arabic where you will need more than duplicated ya‘.

4.0 Conclusion You should note that what ش(cid:13)A and اDCA have in common is the issue of timing; both of them connote a feature occurrence of an event.
However, their difference is in negative and positive meanings; while ش(cid:13)A connotes never to happen اDCA connotes excitement and love for the event or thing to happen.

Introduction ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A is a cluster of letters commonly referred to as in a statement which reads thus: (cid:13)?َْ2(cid:10)َ(cid:8)(cid:19)ُ0ُ(cid:22)ْ@َ(cid:26)َ i.e.
you asked me of them.

Objectives At the end of this unit, you should be able to: • list ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A; • Identify ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A in verb and nouns.

3.0 Main Content 3.1 Huruufuz-ziyaadah are so called because of the role they play in verbs and nouns.
They provide additional letters to what is known in a verb or noun as foundation letters or constituent letters/radicals.
For example, lَ (cid:30)َ(cid:20)َ is known as "!+ د(cid:4).
(cid:14) as already explained to you in the previous modules.
If you add ة5(cid:14) %(cid:22)أ to l(cid:30)(cid:20), you have lَ (cid:22)َ(cid:13)(cid:20)َ while l(cid:30)(cid:20) means (he) sat e.g.
ٌ,(cid:14)ِْr(cid:14)ُ lَ (cid:30)َ(cid:20)َ (Mu’min sat), lَ (cid:22)َ(cid:13)(cid:20)َ means (he) sat with e.g.
ا5ً(cid:22)ِ(cid:13)Vَ ٌ,(cid:14)ِْr(cid:14)ُ lَ (cid:22)َ(cid:13)(cid:20)َ (Mu’min sat with Khalid) in the same token, ٌ(cid:25)(cid:30)َ[َ (a pen) is a د(cid:4).

But in مُ7َ [ْأَ we have ة5(cid:14) %(cid:22)أ which is an additional letter.
It should be noted that ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A are not used for mere aesthetics.
They are employed to create fresh meanings and effects.
As you can see in ٌ(cid:25)(cid:30)َ[َ above, with ة5(cid:14) %(cid:22)أ added, ٌ(cid:25)(cid:30)َ[َ changed to ٌم7َ [ْأَ i.e.
from د(cid:4)(cid:17)(cid:14) to (cid:18)(cid:19)(cid:20).
In the case of lَ (cid:30)َ(cid:20)َ and lَ (cid:22)َ(cid:13)(cid:20)َ , you will note that the effect of sitting alone changed to sitting with someone else.
With the use of ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A therefore, ف(cid:4)(cid:6) provides a mechanic for creating numerous verbs and nouns in response to fresh meanings and effects.
The letters are ten.

4.0 Conclusion You should take note of the fact that the s2(cid:10)أ letters are basically part and parcel of ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A known as (cid:13)?2(cid:10)(cid:8)(cid:19)0(cid:22)@(cid:26).
Their designation as sُ 2ْ(cid:10)َأَ letters is for their specific usage as عر(cid:13)g(cid:19)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A.
5.0 Summary It is necessary to note shaddah when ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا فو(cid:4)A are discussed.
Shaddah means a duplicated letter.
For example, ,َ 2(cid:19)ِ(cid:22)َ(cid:13)!َْ(cid:22)ا بd رَ ƒِ 5ُ(cid:19)ْ (cid:9)َ (cid:22)ْاَ.
The shaddah sign on baa mean that letter baa is doubled or duplicated.
In that case, it serves as ةد(cid:13)&(cid:29)(cid:22)ا ف(cid:4)A.
If, for example, سَ رَدَ to study become سَ رaدَ to teach, letter raa’ is duplicated and the additional raa assumes the position of ةد(cid:13)&ز ف(cid:4)A.
So, any other letter can play that role whenever it is duplicated.

81Module 4: نوز(cid:8)(cid:19)(cid:22)او نز(cid:8)(cid:22)ا Unit 2: (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ 1.0 Introduction 2.0 Objectives 3.0 Main Content 3.1 نوز(cid:8)(cid:19)(cid:22)او نز(cid:8)(cid:22)ا 3.2 (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ 3.3 Illustrations 4.0 Conclusion 5.0 Summary 6.0 Tutor Marked Assignment 7.0 References/Further Reading 5.0 Introduction نوز(cid:8)(cid:19)(cid:22)او نز(cid:8)(cid:22)ا In this unit, my intention is to do what I call a mob up presentation.
This is to recap some of the topics we have treated to give it a fresh treatment.
It is for emphasis and reinforcement.
I am particularly inclined to treating نوز(cid:8)(cid:19)(cid:22)او نز(cid:8)(cid:22)ا as two terms that occupy a special position in ف(cid:4)(cid:6) generally.
The two terms actually deserve this special mention.
Also to be treated specially is (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ.
2.0 Objectives At the end of this unit, you should be able to: • correctly use the terms نوز(cid:8)(cid:19)(cid:22)او نز(cid:8)(cid:22)ا.
• state the differences between "#(cid:13)(cid:17)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ and (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ; and • give illustration.
3.0 نوز(cid:8)(cid:19)(cid:22)او نز(cid:8)(cid:22)ا 3.1 نوز(cid:8)(cid:19)(cid:22)او نز(cid:8)(cid:22)ا is the hup of ف(cid:4)(cid:6).
It cuts across all aspects of Ṣarf.
Every word ((cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)آ) has a Wazn and every Wazn has mawzuun.
It is important that you know how to use the two terms appropriately.
The Wazn means the scale i.e.
the measure used in determining the status of every (cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:30)آ.
For example, ٌ"!ْ+َ is a wazn and the mawzuun is ٌ5ْ#وَ .
You can therefore, ask a question: what is the wazn of ٌ5#ْ وَ ?
Your answer is: ٌ"!ْ+َ is the wazn of ٌ5#ْ وَ .
Furthermore, you can as well ask: what is the mawzuun of ٌ"!ْ+َ?
Its mawzuun is ٌ5#ْ وَ .
The method of determining wazn of a kalmah or mawzuun of a wazn is very simple.
The smallest size of a word in Arabic is the three lettered.
This is called thulaathi.
In other words, no Arabic word is less than three letters.
In case you see a word of two letters or one such as ْ"[ُ (say) or قِ (save), certainly, such a word must have 82been subjected to some structural adjournment exercise by means of elimination of one or two letters for morphological reasons which are explainable.
3.1.1 The starting point of mastering of the technique is through labeling the constituent letters.
You will recall what we term the foundation radicals.
One must reiterate, foundation radicals or constituent letters are the original letters in a verb or noun each of which cannot be removed or else, the word is rendered meaningless.
If, for example you remove a letter from ^ُ ْ(cid:30)آَ, say ك, the remaining ^(cid:22) will be meaningless.
Or you remove a letter from (cid:18)َ (cid:19)ِ(cid:26)َ , say م, the remaining (cid:18)َ (cid:14)ِ will be meaningless.
So, labelling is the game.
The wazn "َ !َ+َ or "ُْ!+َ is labelled as follows: "َ ــــ!َـــ+َ.
ِ"ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُمَ(cid:23) "ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُ,ْ2َ# ِ"ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُء(cid:13)َ+ ِ That of ٌ"!ْ+َ follows the same pattern i.e.
"ُـــ!ْـــ+َ ِ"ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُمَ(cid:23) "ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُ,ْ2َ# ِ"ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُء(cid:13)َ+ ِ When the same pattern is applied to mawzuun, we have the following: lَ ـــ(cid:30)َـــ(cid:20)َ ِ"ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُمَ(cid:23) "ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُ,ْ2َ# ِ"ْ!ِ(cid:17)ْ(cid:22)ا ُء(cid:13)َ+ ِ By now, you must have been able to distinguish wazn from mawzuun.

3.2 (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ This is another language structure designed to create an effect; a special effect.
Literally, (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا means exaggeration.
Technically though, (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا is a special structure meant for creating a special meaning.
In this case, (cid:25)(cid:26)إ is attributed to it as we say (cid:21)B(cid:22)(cid:13)C(cid:19)(cid:22)ا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ which means a noun structured to connote a higher degree of (cid:25)(cid:26)إ "#(cid:13)(cid:17)(cid:22)ا i.e.
the doer e.g.
ٌ^'ِ(cid:13)آَ or ٌ"#ِ (cid:13)+َ.
While ٌ^'ِ(cid:13)آَ means a writer, ٌ"#ِ (cid:13)+َ means a worker 84or a doer.
But when a particular writer (ٌ^'ِ(cid:13)آَ) writes at a rate faster, better more intense than an ordinary writer or when a worker (ٌ"#ِ (cid:13)+َ) works more devotedly, more diligently with an exceeding commitment, the ف(cid:4)(cid:6) comes up with a structure to express that higher level of handling the craft.
Then, you have ٌل(cid:13)!a+َ or ٌب(cid:13)0aآَ.
So ٌل(cid:13)!a+َ or ٌب(cid:13)0aآَ is called (cid:21)ِBَ(cid:22)َ(cid:13)Cَ(cid:19)ُ(cid:22)ْا (cid:25)(cid:26)إ.
3.2.1 As usual in Ṣarf, every structure has a wazn and mawzuun.
